	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Disneyland</h1>

<p><b>Disneyland Park</b>, originally <b>Disneyland</b>, is the first of two <a href="/wiki/Amusement_park" title="Amusement park">theme parks</a> built at the <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Resort" title="Disneyland Resort">Disneyland Resort</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">Anaheim, California</a>, opened on July 17, 1955. It is the only theme park designed and built to completion under the direct supervision of <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney" title="Walt Disney">Walt Disney</a>. It was originally the only attraction on the property; its official name was changed to Disneyland Park to distinguish it from the expanding complex in the 1990s. It is the oldest Disney Park in the world.
</p><p>Walt Disney came up with the concept of Disneyland after visiting various amusement parks with his daughters in the 1930s and 1940s. He initially envisioned building a tourist attraction adjacent to his <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(Burbank)" title="Walt Disney Studios (Burbank)">studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Burbank,_California" title="Burbank, California">Burbank</a> to entertain fans who wished to visit; however, he soon realized that the proposed site was too small. After hiring a consultant to help him determine an appropriate site for his project, Disney bought a 160-acre (65&#160;ha) site near Anaheim in 1953. Construction began in 1954 and the park was unveiled during a special televised press event on the <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> Television Network on July 17, 1955.
</p><p>Since its opening, Disneyland has undergone expansions and major renovations, including the addition of <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Square" title="New Orleans Square">New Orleans Square</a> in 1966, <a href="/wiki/Critter_Country" title="Critter Country">Bear Country</a> (now Critter Country) in 1972,  <a href="/wiki/Mickey%27s_Toontown" title="Mickey&#39;s Toontown">Mickey's Toontown</a> in 1993, and <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galaxy%27s_Edge" title="Star Wars: Galaxy&#39;s Edge"><i>Star Wars</i>: Galaxy's Edge</a> in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Savvas_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Savvas-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Opened in 2001, <a href="/wiki/Disney_California_Adventure" title="Disney California Adventure">Disney California Adventure Park</a> was built on the site of Disneyland's original parking lot.
</p><p>Disneyland has a larger cumulative attendance than any other theme park in the world, with 726 million visits since it opened (as of December 2018). In 2018, the park had approximately 18.6 million visits, making it the second most visited amusement park in the world that year, behind only <a href="/wiki/Magic_Kingdom" title="Magic Kingdom">Magic Kingdom</a>, the very park it inspired.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> According to a March 2005 Disney report, 65,700 jobs are supported by the Disneyland Resort, including about 20,000 direct Disney employees and 3,800 third-party employees (<a href="/wiki/Independent_contractor" title="Independent contractor">independent contractors</a> or their employees).<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Disney announced "Project Stardust" in 2019, which included major structural renovations to the park to account for higher attendance numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:23em;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-title" style="">Original dedication</div>
<div class="quotebox-quote center-aligned" style="">To all who come to this happy place: Welcome. Disneyland is your land. Here age relives fond memories of the past, and here youth may savor the challenge and promise of the future. Disneyland is dedicated to the ideals, the dreams, and the hard facts that have created America, with the hope that it will be a source of joy and inspiration to all the world.</div>
<p><cite class="center-aligned" style=""><a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney" title="Walt Disney">Walter E. Disney</a>, July 17, 1955<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WaltDisneyplansDisneylandDec1954.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Walt Disney with Orange County officials" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/WaltDisneyplansDisneylandDec1954.jpg/220px-WaltDisneyplansDisneylandDec1954.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/WaltDisneyplansDisneylandDec1954.jpg/330px-WaltDisneyplansDisneylandDec1954.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/WaltDisneyplansDisneylandDec1954.jpg/440px-WaltDisneyplansDisneylandDec1954.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2723" data-file-height="2417" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WaltDisneyplansDisneylandDec1954.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Walt Disney (center) showing Orange County officials plans for Disneyland's layout, December 1954</div></div></div>
<p>The concept for Disneyland began when Walt Disney was visiting <a href="/wiki/Griffith_Park" title="Griffith Park">Griffith Park</a> in Los Angeles with his daughters Diane and Sharon. While watching them ride the <a href="/wiki/Merry-go-round" class="mw-redirect" title="Merry-go-round">merry-go-round</a>, he came up with the idea of a place where adults and their children could go and have fun together, though his dream lay dormant for many years.<sup id="cite_ref-Dreaming_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dreaming-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He may have also been influenced by his father's memories of the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Columbian_Exposition" title="World&#39;s Columbian Exposition">World's Columbian Exposition</a> of 1893 in Chicago (his father worked at the Exposition). The <a href="/wiki/Midway_Plaisance" title="Midway Plaisance">Midway Plaisance</a> there included a set of attractions representing various countries from around the world and others representing various periods of man; it also included many rides including the first <a href="/wiki/Ferris_wheel" title="Ferris wheel">Ferris wheel</a>, a "sky" ride, a passenger train that circled the perimeter, and a Wild West Show. Another likely influence was <a href="/wiki/Benton_Harbor,_Michigan" title="Benton Harbor, Michigan">Benton Harbor, Michigan</a>'s nationally famous <a href="/wiki/House_of_David_(commune)" title="House of David (commune)">House of David</a>'s Eden Springs Park. Disney visited the park and ultimately bought one of the older miniature trains originally used there; the colony had the largest miniature railway setup in the world at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The earliest documented draft of Disney's plans was sent as a memo to studio production designer Dick Kelsey on August 31, 1948, where it was referred to as a "Mickey Mouse Park", based on notes Disney made during his and <a href="/wiki/Ward_Kimball" title="Ward Kimball">Ward Kimball</a>'s trip to <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Railroad_Fair" title="Chicago Railroad Fair">Chicago Railroad Fair</a> the same month, with a two-day stop in
<a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry Ford</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Henry_Ford" title="The Henry Ford">Museum and Greenfield Village</a>, a place with attractions like a Main Street and steamboat rides, which he had visited eight years earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While people wrote letters to Disney about visiting the <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(Burbank)" title="Walt Disney Studios (Burbank)">Walt Disney Studios</a>, he realized that a functional movie studio had little to offer to visiting fans, and began to foster ideas of building a site near the Burbank studios for tourists to visit. His ideas evolved to a small play park with a boat ride and other themed areas. The initial concept, the Mickey Mouse Park, started with an 3.2-hectare (8-acre) plot across Riverside Drive. He started to visit other parks for inspiration and ideas, including <a href="/wiki/Tivoli_Gardens,_Copenhagen" class="mw-redirect" title="Tivoli Gardens, Copenhagen">Tivoli Gardens</a> in Denmark, <a href="/wiki/Efteling" title="Efteling">Efteling</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, and Greenfield Village, <a href="/wiki/Playland_(San_Francisco)" title="Playland (San Francisco)">Playland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Fairyland" title="Children&#39;s Fairyland">Children's Fairyland</a> in the United States; and (according to the film director Ken Annakin, in his autobiography 'So You want to be a film director?'), Bekonscot Model Village &amp; Railway, Beaconsfield, England. His designers began working on concepts, though the project grew much larger than the land could hold.<sup id="cite_ref-JustDisney_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JustDisney-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Disney hired <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Price" title="Harrison Price">Harrison Price</a> from <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Research_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanford Research Institute">Stanford Research Institute</a> to gauge the proper area to locate the theme park based on the area's potential growth. Based on Price's analysis (for which he would be recognized as a <a href="/wiki/Disney_Legends" title="Disney Legends">Disney Legend</a> in 2003), Disney acquired 65&#160;ha (160 acres) of orange groves and walnut trees in Anaheim, southeast of Los Angeles in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JustDisney_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JustDisney-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-harrison_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harrison-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The Burbank site originally considered by Disney is now home to <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Animation_Studios" title="Walt Disney Animation Studios">Walt Disney Animation Studios</a> and <a href="/wiki/ABC_Studios" title="ABC Studios">ABC Studios</a>.
</p><p>Difficulties in obtaining funding prompted Disney to investigate new methods of fundraising, and he decided to create a show named <i><a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_anthology_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Walt Disney anthology series">Disneyland</a>.</i> It was broadcast on then-fledgling <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>. In return, the network agreed to help finance the park. For its first five years of operation, Disneyland was owned by <a href="/wiki/Disneyland,_Inc." title="Disneyland, Inc.">Disneyland, Inc.</a>, which was jointly owned by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Productions" class="mw-redirect" title="Walt Disney Productions">Walt Disney Productions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney" title="Walt Disney">Walt Disney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Publishing" title="Western Publishing">Western Publishing</a> and ABC.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Disney rented out many of the shops on Main Street, U.S.A. to outside companies. By 1960, Walt Disney Productions bought out all other shares, a partnership which would eventually lead to the Walt Disney Corporation's acquisition of ABC in the mid-1990s. Construction began on July 16, 1954 and cost $17 million to complete. The park was opened one year and one day later.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_101" title="U.S. Route 101">U.S. Route 101</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Interstate_5" title="Interstate 5">Interstate 5</a>) was under construction at the same time just north of the site; in preparation for the traffic Disneyland was expected to bring, two more lanes were added to the freeway before the park was finished.<sup id="cite_ref-harrison_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harrison-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_day">Opening day</span></h4>
<p>Disneyland was dedicated at an "International Press Preview" event held on Sunday, July 17, 1955, which was open only to invited guests and the media. Although 28,000 people attended the event, only about half of those were invitees, the rest having purchased counterfeit tickets,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> or even sneaked into the park by climbing over the fence.<sup id="cite_ref-KorkisOpeningDay_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KorkisOpeningDay-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The following day, it opened to the public, featuring twenty attractions. The Special Sunday events, including the dedication, were televised nationwide and anchored by three of Walt Disney's friends from Hollywood: <a href="/wiki/Art_Linkletter" title="Art Linkletter">Art Linkletter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Cummings" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Cummings">Bob Cummings</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>. ABC broadcast the event live, during which many guests tripped over the television camera cables.<sup id="cite_ref-koening2006_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-koening2006-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In Frontierland, a camera caught Cummings kissing a dancer. When Disney started to read the plaque for Tomorrowland, he read partway then stopped when a technician off-camera said something to him, and after realizing he was on-air, said, "I thought I got a signal",<sup id="cite_ref-koening2006_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-koening2006-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and began the dedication from the start. At one point, while in Fantasyland, Linkletter tried to give coverage to Cummings, who was on the pirate ship. He was not ready, and tried to give the coverage back to Linkletter, who had lost his microphone. Cummings then did a play-by-play of him trying to find it in front of Mr. Toad's Wild Ride.<sup id="cite_ref-koening2006_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-koening2006-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Traffic was delayed on the two-lane Harbor Boulevard.<sup id="cite_ref-koening2006_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-koening2006-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Famous figures who were scheduled to show up every two hours showed up all at once. The temperature was an unusually high 38&#160;°C (101&#160;°F), and because of a local plumbers' strike, Disney was given a choice of having working drinking fountains or running toilets. He chose the latter, leaving many drinking fountains dry. This generated negative publicity since <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> sponsored the park's opening; disappointed guests believed the inoperable fountains were a cynical way to sell soda, while other vendors ran out of food. The asphalt that had been poured that morning was soft enough to let women's high-heeled shoes sink into it. Some parents threw their children over the crowd's shoulders to get them onto rides, such as the <a href="/wiki/King_Arthur_Carrousel" title="King Arthur Carrousel">King Arthur Carrousel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In later years, Disney and his 1955 executives referred to July 17, 1955, as "Black Sunday". After the extremely negative press from the preview opening, Walt Disney invited attendees back for a private "second day" to experience Disneyland properly.
</p><p>At the time, and during the lifetimes of Walt and Roy Disney, July 17 was considered merely a preview, with July 18 the official opening day.<sup id="cite_ref-KorkisOpeningDay_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KorkisOpeningDay-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Since then, aided by memories of the television broadcast, the company has adopted July 17 as the official date, the one commemorated every year as Disneyland's birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-KorkisOpeningDay_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KorkisOpeningDay-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1950s_and_1960s">1950s and 1960s</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:6308-AnaheimDisneyLand-NW_to_SE_View.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/6308-AnaheimDisneyLand-NW_to_SE_View.jpg/220px-6308-AnaheimDisneyLand-NW_to_SE_View.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/6308-AnaheimDisneyLand-NW_to_SE_View.jpg/330px-6308-AnaheimDisneyLand-NW_to_SE_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/6308-AnaheimDisneyLand-NW_to_SE_View.jpg/440px-6308-AnaheimDisneyLand-NW_to_SE_View.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1802" data-file-height="1110" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:6308-AnaheimDisneyLand-NW_to_SE_View.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Disneyland aerial view, 1963, which includes the new Melody Land Theater at the top of the photo</div></div></div>
<p>In September 1959, Soviet First Secretary <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> spent thirteen days in the United States, with two requests: to visit Disneyland and to meet <a href="/wiki/John_Wayne" title="John Wayne">John Wayne</a>, Hollywood's top box-office draw. Due to the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> tension and security concerns, he was famously denied an excursion to Disneyland.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi" title="Mohammad Reza Pahlavi">The Shah of Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Empress_Farah" class="mw-redirect" title="Empress Farah">Empress Farah</a> were invited to Disneyland by Walt Disney in the early 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> There was moderate controversy over the lack of African American employees. As late as 1963, <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil rights">civil rights</a> activists were pressuring Disneyland to hire black people,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> with executives responding that they would "consider" the requests.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This information is not in the source for the previous clause. It might be in the Galber source cited in the following sentence, but if so the formatting is awkward and should probabky be rewritten so that each source supports the sentence to which it is attached. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The park did however hire <a href="/wiki/Asian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian American">people of Asian descent</a>, such as Ty Wong and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Kuwahara" title="Bob Kuwahara">Bob Kuwahara</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As part of the Casa de Fritos operation at Disneyland, "<a href="/wiki/Doritos" title="Doritos">Doritos</a>" (Spanish for "little golden things") were created at the park to recycle old tortillas that would have been discarded. The Frito-Lay Company saw the popularity of the item and began selling them regionally in 1964, and then nationwide in 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span></h4>
<p>On December 5, 1985, to celebrate Disneyland's 30th year in operation, one million balloons were launched along the streets bordering Disneyland as part of the <a href="/wiki/Skyfest_Celebration" title="Skyfest Celebration">Skyfest Celebration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span></h4>
<p>In the late 1990s, work began to expand the one-park, one-hotel property. Disneyland Park, the Disneyland Hotel, the site of the original parking lot, and acquired surrounding properties were earmarked to become part of the <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Resort" title="Disneyland Resort">Disneyland Resort</a>. At that time, the property saw the addition of the <a href="/wiki/Disney_California_Adventure" title="Disney California Adventure">Disney California Adventure</a> theme park, a shopping, dining and entertainment complex named <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Disney_(California)" class="mw-redirect" title="Downtown Disney (California)">Downtown Disney</a>, a remodeled <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Hotel_(California)" title="Disneyland Hotel (California)">Disneyland Hotel</a>, the construction of <a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Grand_Californian_Hotel_%26_Spa" title="Disney&#39;s Grand Californian Hotel &amp; Spa">Disney's Grand Californian Hotel &amp; Spa</a>, and the acquisition and re-branding of the Pan Pacific Hotel as <a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Paradise_Pier_Hotel" title="Disney&#39;s Paradise Pier Hotel">Disney's Paradise Pier Hotel</a>. The park was renamed "Disneyland Park" to distinguish it from the larger complex under construction. Because the existing parking lot (south of Disneyland) was repurposed by these projects, the six-level, 10,250-space Mickey and Friends parking structure was constructed in the northwest corner. Upon completion in 2000, it was the largest parking structure in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The park's management team during the mid-1990s was a source of controversy among fans and employees. In an effort to boost profits, various changes were begun by then-executives <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_Harriss" title="Cynthia Harriss">Cynthia Harriss</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Pressler" title="Paul Pressler">Paul Pressler</a>. While their initiatives provided a short-term increase in shareholder returns, they drew widespread criticism for their lack of foresight. The retail backgrounds of Harriss and Pressler led to a gradual shift in Disneyland's focus from attractions to merchandising. Outside consultants <a href="/wiki/McKinsey_%26_Company" title="McKinsey &amp; Company">McKinsey &amp; Company</a> were brought in to help streamline operations, resulting in many changes and cutbacks. After nearly a decade of deferred maintenance, the original park was showing signs of neglect. Fans of the park decried the perceived decline in customer value and park quality and rallied for the dismissal of the management team.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Disneyland_Anaheim.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Disneyland in 2005" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Disneyland_Anaheim.jpg/220px-Disneyland_Anaheim.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Disneyland_Anaheim.jpg/330px-Disneyland_Anaheim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Disneyland_Anaheim.jpg/440px-Disneyland_Anaheim.jpg 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="657" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Disneyland_Anaheim.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An aerial view of Disneyland in 2004</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Matt_Ouimet" title="Matt Ouimet">Matt Ouimet</a>, the former president of the <a href="/wiki/Disney_Cruise_Line" title="Disney Cruise Line">Disney Cruise Line</a>, was promoted to assume leadership of the Disneyland Resort in late 2003. Shortly afterward, he selected <a href="/wiki/Greg_Emmer" title="Greg Emmer">Greg Emmer</a> as Senior Vice President of Operations. Emmer was a long-time Disney cast member who had worked at Disneyland in his youth prior to moving to Florida and held multiple executive leadership positions at the <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World" title="Walt Disney World">Walt Disney World Resort</a>. Ouimet quickly set about reversing certain trends, especially concerning cosmetic maintenance and a return to the original infrastructure maintenance schedule, in hopes of restoring Disneyland's former safety record. Similarly to Disney himself, Ouimet and Emmer could often be seen walking the park during business hours with members of their respective staff, wearing cast member name badges, standing in line for attractions, and welcoming guests' comments. In July 2006, Ouimet left The Walt Disney Company to become president of <a href="/wiki/Starwood_Hotels_%26_Resorts_Worldwide" class="mw-redirect" title="Starwood Hotels &amp; Resorts Worldwide">Starwood Hotels &amp; Resorts Worldwide</a>. Soon after, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Grier" title="Ed Grier">Ed Grier</a>, executive managing director of Walt Disney Attractions Japan, was named president of the resort. In October 2009, Grier announced his retirement, and was replaced by George Kalogridis.
</p><p>The "<a href="/wiki/Happiest_Homecoming_on_Earth" title="Happiest Homecoming on Earth">Happiest Homecoming on Earth</a>" was an eighteen-month-long celebration (held through 2005 and 2006) of the fiftieth anniversary of the Disneyland Park, also celebrating Disneyland's milestone throughout Disney parks worldwide. In 2004, the park underwent major renovations in preparation, restoring many attractions, notably <a href="/wiki/Space_Mountain_(Disneyland)" title="Space Mountain (Disneyland)">Space Mountain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jungle_Cruise" title="Jungle Cruise">Jungle Cruise</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Haunted_Mansion" class="mw-redirect" title="Haunted Mansion">Haunted Mansion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(attraction)" title="Pirates of the Caribbean (attraction)">Pirates of the Caribbean</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney%27s_Enchanted_Tiki_Room" title="Walt Disney&#39;s Enchanted Tiki Room">Walt Disney's Enchanted Tiki Room</a>. Attractions that had been in the park on opening day had one ride vehicle painted gold, and the park was decorated with fifty <a href="/wiki/Hidden_Mickey_50_Ears" class="mw-redirect" title="Hidden Mickey 50 Ears">Golden Mickey Ears</a>. The celebration started on May 5, 2005, and ended on September 30, 2006, and was followed by the "Year of a Million Dreams" celebration, lasting twenty-seven months and ending on December 31, 2008.
</p><p>Beginning on January 1, 2010, Disney Parks hosted the <a href="/wiki/Give_a_Day,_Get_a_Disney_Day" title="Give a Day, Get a Disney Day">Give a Day, Get a Disney Day</a> volunteer program, in which Disney encouraged people to volunteer with a participating charity and receive a free Disney Day at either a Disneyland Resort or Walt Disney World park. On March 9, 2010, Disney announced that it had reached its goal of one million volunteers and ended the promotion to anyone who had not yet registered and signed up for a specific volunteer situation.
</p><p>In July 2015, Disneyland celebrated its 60th <i>Diamond Celebration</i> anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Disneyland Park introduced the <a href="/wiki/Paint_the_Night" title="Paint the Night">Paint the Night</a> parade and <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Forever" title="Disneyland Forever">Disneyland Forever</a> fireworks show, and <a href="/wiki/Sleeping_Beauty_Castle" title="Sleeping Beauty Castle">Sleeping Beauty Castle</a> is decorated in diamonds with a large "60" logo. The Diamond Celebration concluded in September 2016 and the whole decoration of the anniversary was removed around Halloween 2016.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lands">Lands</span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Disneyland&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Disneyland%22">"Disneyland"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Disneyland%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Disneyland%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Disneyland%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Disneyland%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Disneyland%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Disneyland_attractions" title="List of Disneyland attractions">List of Disneyland attractions</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_former_Disneyland_attractions" title="List of former Disneyland attractions">List of former Disneyland attractions</a></div>
<p>Disneyland Park consists of nine themed "lands" and a number of concealed backstage areas, and occupies over 40&#160;ha (100 acres) with the new addition of Mickey and Minnie's Runaway Railway that's coming to Mickeys Toontown in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-JustDisney_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JustDisney-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The park opened with <a href="/wiki/Main_Street,_U.S.A." title="Main Street, U.S.A.">Main Street, U.S.A.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adventureland_(Disney)" title="Adventureland (Disney)">Adventureland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frontierland" title="Frontierland">Frontierland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fantasyland" title="Fantasyland">Fantasyland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tomorrowland" title="Tomorrowland">Tomorrowland</a>, and has since added <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Square" title="New Orleans Square">New Orleans Square</a> in 1966, Bear Country (now known as <a href="/wiki/Critter_Country" title="Critter Country">Critter Country</a>) in 1972, and <a href="/wiki/Mickey%27s_Toontown" title="Mickey&#39;s Toontown">Mickey's Toontown</a> in 1993, and <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galaxy%27s_Edge" title="Star Wars: Galaxy&#39;s Edge"><i>Star Wars</i>: Galaxy's Edge</a> in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In 1957, <a href="/wiki/Holidayland_(Disneyland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Holidayland (Disneyland)">Holidayland</a> opened to the public with a 3.6-hectare (9-acre) recreation area including a <a href="/wiki/Circus" title="Circus">circus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baseball_diamond" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball diamond">baseball diamond</a>, but was closed in late 1961. It is often referred to as the "lost" land of Disneyland. Throughout the park are "<a href="/wiki/Hidden_Mickey" title="Hidden Mickey">Hidden Mickeys</a>", representations of Mickey Mouse heads inserted subtly into the design of attractions and environmental decor. An elevated <a href="/wiki/Berm" title="Berm">berm</a> supports the <a href="/wiki/3_ft_gauge_railways" title="3 ft gauge railways"><span class="nowrap">3&#160;ft</span></a> (<span class="nowrap">914&#160;mm</span>) <a href="/wiki/Narrow_gauge_railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Narrow gauge railway">narrow gauge</a> <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Railroad" title="Disneyland Railroad">Disneyland Railroad</a> that circumnavigates the park.
</p>

<h3><span id="Main_Street.2C_U.S.A."></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_Street,_U.S.A.">Main Street, U.S.A.</span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Disneyland&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Disneyland%22">"Disneyland"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Disneyland%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Disneyland%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Disneyland%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Disneyland%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Disneyland%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Main_Street,_U.S.A." title="Main Street, U.S.A.">Main Street, U.S.A.</a></div>
<p>Main Street, U.S.A. is patterned after a typical <a href="/wiki/Midwest" class="mw-redirect" title="Midwest">Midwest</a> town of the early 20th century. Main Street, U.S.A. has a train station, town square, movie theater, city hall, firehouse with a steam-powered pump engine, emporium, shops, arcades, double-decker bus, horse-drawn streetcar, and jitneys. Main Street is also home to the Disney Art Gallery and the Opera House which showcases <i><a href="/wiki/Great_Moments_with_Mr._Lincoln" title="Great Moments with Mr. Lincoln">Great Moments with Mr. Lincoln</a></i>, a show featuring an <a href="/wiki/Audio-Animatronic" class="mw-redirect" title="Audio-Animatronic">Audio-Animatronic</a> version of the president. At the far end of Main Street, U.S.A. is <a href="/wiki/Sleeping_Beauty_Castle" title="Sleeping Beauty Castle">Sleeping Beauty Castle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Partners_(statue)" title="Partners (statue)"><i>Partners</i> statue</a>, and the Central Plaza (also known as the Hub), which is a portal to most of the themed lands: the entrance to <a href="/wiki/Fantasyland" title="Fantasyland">Fantasyland</a> is by way of a drawbridge across a moat and through the castle. <a href="/wiki/Adventureland_(Disney)" title="Adventureland (Disney)">Adventureland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frontierland" title="Frontierland">Frontierland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tomorrowland" title="Tomorrowland">Tomorrowland</a> are on both sides of the castle. Several lands are not directly connected to the Central Plaza—namely, <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Square" title="New Orleans Square">New Orleans Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Critter_Country" title="Critter Country">Critter Country</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mickey%27s_Toontown" title="Mickey&#39;s Toontown">Mickey's Toontown</a>.
</p><p>The design of Main Street, U.S.A. uses the technique of <a href="/wiki/Forced_perspective" title="Forced perspective">forced perspective</a> to create an illusion of height. Buildings along Main Street are built at &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>3</sup>&#8260;<sub>4</sub></span> scale on the first level, then &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>5</sup>&#8260;<sub>8</sub></span> on the second story, and &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>2</sub></span> scale on the third—reducing the scale by &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>8</sub></span> each level up.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adventureland">Adventureland</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Adventureland_(Disney)" title="Adventureland (Disney)">Adventureland (Disney)</a></div>
<p>Adventureland is designed to recreate the feel of an exotic tropical place in a far-off region of the world. "To create a land that would make this dream reality", said Walt Disney, "we pictured ourselves far from civilization, in the remote <a href="/wiki/Jungle" title="Jungle">jungles</a> of Asia and Africa." Attractions include opening day's <a href="/wiki/Jungle_Cruise" title="Jungle Cruise">Jungle Cruise</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indiana_Jones_Adventure" title="Indiana Jones Adventure">Indiana Jones Adventure</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tarzan%27s_Treehouse" title="Tarzan&#39;s Treehouse">Tarzan's Treehouse</a>, which is a conversion of <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Family_Treehouse" title="Swiss Family Treehouse">Swiss Family Treehouse</a> from the Walt Disney film <i><a href="/wiki/Swiss_Family_Robinson_(1960_film)" title="Swiss Family Robinson (1960 film)">Swiss Family Robinson</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney%27s_Enchanted_Tiki_Room" title="Walt Disney&#39;s Enchanted Tiki Room">Walt Disney's Enchanted Tiki Room</a> which is located at the entrance to Adventureland was the first feature attraction to employ <a href="/wiki/Audio-Animatronics" title="Audio-Animatronics">Audio-Animatronics</a>, a computer synchronization of sound and robotics.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Orleans_Square">New Orleans Square</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Square" title="New Orleans Square">New Orleans Square</a></div>
<p>New Orleans Square is based on 19th-century <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>, opened on July 24, 1966. It is home to <a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(theme_park_ride)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirates of the Caribbean (theme park ride)">Pirates of the Caribbean</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Haunted_Mansion" class="mw-redirect" title="Haunted Mansion">Haunted Mansion</a>, with nighttime entertainment in <i><a href="/wiki/Fantasmic!" title="Fantasmic!">Fantasmic!</a></i>. This area is the home of <a href="/wiki/Club_33" title="Club 33">Club 33</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frontierland">Frontierland</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Frontierland" title="Frontierland">Frontierland</a></div>
<p>Frontierland recreates the setting of pioneer days along the <a href="/wiki/American_frontier" title="American frontier">American frontier</a>. According to Walt Disney, "All of us have cause to be proud of our country's history, shaped by the pioneering spirit of our forefathers. Our adventures are designed to give you the feeling of having lived, even for a short while, during our country's pioneer days." Frontierland is home to the Pinewood Indians band of animatronic Native Americans, who live on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Rivers_of_America_(Disney)" title="Rivers of America (Disney)">Rivers of America</a>. Entertainment and attractions include <a href="/wiki/Big_Thunder_Mountain_Railroad" title="Big Thunder Mountain Railroad">Big Thunder Mountain Railroad</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mark_Twain_Riverboat" title="Mark Twain Riverboat">Mark Twain Riverboat</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sailing_Ship_Columbia" title="Sailing Ship Columbia">Sailing Ship Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pirate%27s_Lair_on_Tom_Sawyer_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirate&#39;s Lair on Tom Sawyer Island">Pirate's Lair on Tom Sawyer Island</a>, and Frontierland Shootin' Exposition. Frontierland is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horseshoe_Saloon" title="Golden Horseshoe Saloon">Golden Horseshoe Saloon</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Old_West" class="mw-redirect" title="Old West">Old West</a>-style show palace.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critter_Country">Critter Country</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Critter_Country" title="Critter Country">Critter Country</a></div>
<p>Critter Country opened in 1972 as "Bear Country", and was renamed in 1988. Formerly the area was home to Indian Village, where indigenous tribespeople demonstrated their dances and other customs. Today, the main draw of the area is <a href="/wiki/Splash_Mountain" title="Splash Mountain">Splash Mountain</a>, a log-flume journey inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Remus" title="Uncle Remus">Uncle Remus</a> stories of <a href="/wiki/Joel_Chandler_Harris" title="Joel Chandler Harris">Joel Chandler Harris</a> and the animated segments of Disney's Academy Award-winning 1946 film <i><a href="/wiki/Song_of_the_South" title="Song of the South">Song of the South</a></i>. In 2003, a <a href="/wiki/Dark_ride" title="Dark ride">dark ride</a> called <a href="/wiki/The_Many_Adventures_of_Winnie_the_Pooh_(attraction)" title="The Many Adventures of Winnie the Pooh (attraction)">The Many Adventures of Winnie the Pooh</a> replaced the <a href="/wiki/Country_Bear_Jamboree" title="Country Bear Jamboree">Country Bear Jamboree</a>, which closed in 2001. Country Bear Jamboree is still open in Walt Disney World's <a href="/wiki/Magic_Kingdom" title="Magic Kingdom">Magic Kingdom</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Star_Wars:_Galaxy.27s_Edge"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Star_Wars:_Galaxy's_Edge"><i>Star Wars</i>: Galaxy's Edge</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galaxy%27s_Edge" title="Star Wars: Galaxy&#39;s Edge">Star Wars: Galaxy's Edge</a></div>
<p><i>Star Wars</i>: Galaxy's Edge is set within the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> universe, in the Black Spire Outpost village on the remote frontier planet of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Star_Wars_planets_and_moons" title="List of Star Wars planets and moons">Batuu</a>. Attractions include the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Falcon:_Smugglers_Run" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Falcon: Smugglers Run">Millennium Falcon: Smugglers Run</a> and <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Rise_of_the_Resistance" title="Star Wars: Rise of the Resistance"><i>Star Wars</i>: Rise of the Resistance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Disney_Parks_Blog_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disney_Parks_Blog-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The land opened in 2019, replacing <a href="/wiki/Big_Thunder_Ranch" title="Big Thunder Ranch">Big Thunder Ranch</a> and former backstage areas.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fantasyland">Fantasyland</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fantasyland" title="Fantasyland">Fantasyland</a></div>
<p>Fantasyland is the area of Disneyland of which Walt Disney said, "What youngster has not dreamed of flying with <a href="/wiki/Peter_Pan" title="Peter Pan">Peter Pan</a> over moonlit London, or tumbling into Alice's nonsensical <a href="/wiki/Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland" title="Alice&#39;s Adventures in Wonderland">Wonderland</a>? In Fantasyland, these classic stories of everyone's youth have become realities for youngsters&#160;– of all ages&#160;– to participate in." Fantasyland was originally styled in a medieval European fairground fashion, but its 1983 refurbishment turned it into a <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavarian</a> village. Attractions include several <a href="/wiki/Dark_ride" title="Dark ride">dark rides</a>, the <a href="/wiki/King_Arthur_Carrousel" title="King Arthur Carrousel">King Arthur Carrousel</a>, and various family attractions. Fantasyland has the most <a href="/wiki/Fiber_optics" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiber optics">fiber optics</a> in the park; more than half of them are in <a href="/wiki/Peter_Pan%27s_Flight" title="Peter Pan&#39;s Flight">Peter Pan's Flight</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Sleeping Beauty's Castle features a walk-through story telling of Briar Rose's adventure as Sleeping Beauty. The attraction opened in 1959, was redesigned in 1972, closed in 1992 for reasons of security and the new installation of pneumatic ram firework shell mortars for "Believe, There's Magic in the Stars", and reopened 2008 with new renditions and methods of storytelling and the restored work of <a href="/wiki/Eyvind_Earle" title="Eyvind Earle">Eyvind Earle</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Mickey.27s_Toontown"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mickey's_Toontown">Mickey's Toontown</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mickey%27s_Toontown" title="Mickey&#39;s Toontown">Mickey's Toontown</a></div>
<p>Mickey's Toontown opened in 1993 and was partly inspired by the fictional Los Angeles suburb of Toontown in the <a href="/wiki/Touchstone_Pictures" title="Touchstone Pictures">Touchstone Pictures</a> 1988 release <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Framed_Roger_Rabbit" title="Who Framed Roger Rabbit">Who Framed Roger Rabbit</a></i>. Mickey's Toontown is based on a 1930s cartoon aesthetic and is home to Disney's most popular cartoon characters. Toontown features two main attractions: <a href="/wiki/Gadget%27s_Go_Coaster" title="Gadget&#39;s Go Coaster">Gadget's Go Coaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roger_Rabbit%27s_Car_Toon_Spin" title="Roger Rabbit&#39;s Car Toon Spin">Roger Rabbit's Car Toon Spin</a>. The "city" is also home to cartoon character's houses such as the house of <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Mouse" title="Mickey Mouse">Mickey Mouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnie_Mouse" title="Minnie Mouse">Minnie Mouse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goofy" title="Goofy">Goofy</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Donald_Duck" title="Donald Duck">Donald Duck</a>'s boat. The <span class="nowrap">3&#160;ft</span> (<span class="nowrap">914&#160;mm</span>) gauge <a href="/wiki/Mickey%27s_Toontown#Disneyland" title="Mickey&#39;s Toontown">Jolly Trolley</a> can also be found in this area, though it closed as an attraction in 2003 and is now present only for display purposes. In 2022 <a href="/wiki/Mickey_%26_Minnie%27s_Runaway_Railway" title="Mickey &amp; Minnie&#39;s Runaway Railway">Mickey &amp; Minnie's Runaway Railway</a> will open at Mickey's Toontown. The new family friendly dark ride will increase the size of Toontown as well as the size of Disneyland from 99 acres to 101.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tomorrowland">Tomorrowland</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tomorrowland" title="Tomorrowland">Tomorrowland</a></div>
<p>During the 1955 inauguration Walt Disney dedicated Tomorrowland with these words: "Tomorrow can be a wonderful age. Our scientists today are opening the doors of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Age" title="Space Age">Space Age</a> to achievements that will benefit our children and generations to come. The Tomorrowland attractions have been designed to give you an opportunity to participate in adventures that are a living blueprint of our future."
</p><p>Disneyland producer Ward Kimball had <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_engineering" title="Aerospace engineering">rocket scientists</a> <a href="/wiki/Wernher_von_Braun" title="Wernher von Braun">Wernher von Braun</a>, Willy Ley, and Heinz Haber serve as technical consultants during the original design of Tomorrowland.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Initial attractions included <a href="/wiki/Mission_to_Mars_(attraction)" title="Mission to Mars (attraction)"><i>Rocket to the Moon</i></a>, Astro-Jets and <a href="/wiki/Autopia" title="Autopia">Autopia</a>; later, the first incarnation of the <a href="/wiki/Submarine_Voyage" title="Submarine Voyage">Submarine Voyage</a> was added. The area underwent a major transformation in 1967 to become <i>New Tomorrowland</i>, and then again in 1998 when its focus was changed to present a "retro-future" theme reminiscent of the illustrations of <a href="/wiki/Jules_Verne" title="Jules Verne">Jules Verne</a>.
</p><p>Current attractions include <a href="/wiki/Space_Mountain_(Disneyland)" title="Space Mountain (Disneyland)">Space Mountain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Launch_Bay" title="Star Wars Launch Bay">Star Wars Launch Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autopia" title="Autopia">Autopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jedi_Training:_Trials_of_the_Temple" title="Jedi Training: Trials of the Temple">Jedi Training: Trials of the Temple</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Monorail" class="mw-redirect" title="Disneyland Monorail">Disneyland Monorail</a> Tomorrowland Station, <a href="/wiki/Astro_Orbiter" title="Astro Orbiter">Astro Orbitor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Lightyear_attractions" class="mw-redirect" title="Buzz Lightyear attractions">Buzz Lightyear Astro Blasters</a>. <a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo_Submarine_Voyage" title="Finding Nemo Submarine Voyage">Finding Nemo Submarine Voyage</a> opened on June 11, 2007, resurrecting the original Submarine Voyage which closed in 1998. <a href="/wiki/Star_Tours" title="Star Tours">Star Tours</a> was closed in July 2010 and replaced with <a href="/wiki/Star_Tours%E2%80%93The_Adventures_Continue" class="mw-redirect" title="Star Tours–The Adventures Continue">Star Tours–The Adventures Continue</a> in June 2011.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Backstage">Backstage</span></h3>
<table class="box-No_footnotes plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-No_footnotes" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/60px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/80px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section includes a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">list of references</a>, related reading or <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links" title="Wikipedia:External links">external links</a>, <b>but its sources remain unclear because it lacks <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">inline citations</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Fact_and_Reference_Check" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Fact and Reference Check">improve</a> this section by <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:When_to_cite" title="Wikipedia:When to cite">introducing</a> more precise citations.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2010</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Major buildings backstage include the <a href="/wiki/Frank_Gehry" title="Frank Gehry">Frank Gehry</a>-designed <a href="/wiki/Team_Disney_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Team Disney Anaheim">Team Disney Anaheim</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> where most of the division's administration currently works, as well as the Old Administration Building, behind Tomorrowland.
</p><p>Photography is forbidden in these areas, both inside and outside, although some photos have found their way to a variety of web sites. Guests who attempt to explore backstage are warned and often escorted from the property.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DisneylandTrainLocomotive.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Disneyland Railroad" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/DisneylandTrainLocomotive.jpg/220px-DisneylandTrainLocomotive.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/DisneylandTrainLocomotive.jpg/330px-DisneylandTrainLocomotive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/DisneylandTrainLocomotive.jpg/440px-DisneylandTrainLocomotive.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DisneylandTrainLocomotive.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Disneyland Railroad Engine 2</div></div></div>
<p>Walt Disney had a longtime interest in transportation, and trains in particular. Disney's passion for the "iron horse" led to him building a miniature <a href="/wiki/Live_steam" title="Live steam">live steam</a> <a href="/wiki/Backyard_railroad" title="Backyard railroad">backyard railroad</a>—the "<a href="/wiki/Carolwood_Pacific_Railroad" title="Carolwood Pacific Railroad">Carolwood Pacific Railroad</a>"—on the grounds of his <a href="/wiki/Holmby_Hills,_Los_Angeles,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Holmby Hills, Los Angeles, California">Holmby Hills</a> estate. Throughout all the iterations of Disneyland during the seventeen or so years when Disney was conceiving it, one element remained constant: a train encircling the park.<sup id="cite_ref-Dreaming_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dreaming-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The primary designer for the park transportation vehicles was <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gurr" title="Bob Gurr">Bob Gurr</a> who gave himself the title of Director of Special Vehicle Design in 1954.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Encircling Disneyland and providing a grand circle tour is the <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Railroad" title="Disneyland Railroad">Disneyland Railroad</a> (DRR), a <span class="nowrap">3&#160;ft</span> (<span class="nowrap">914&#160;mm</span>) narrow gauge short-line railway consisting of five oil-fired and steam-powered locomotives, in addition to three passenger trains and one passenger-carrying freight train. Originally known as the Disneyland and Santa Fe Railroad, the DRR was presented by the <a href="/wiki/Atchison,_Topeka_and_Santa_Fe_Railway" title="Atchison, Topeka and Santa Fe Railway">Atchison, Topeka and Santa Fe Railway</a> until 1974. From 1955 to 1974, the Santa Fe Rail Pass was accepted in lieu of a Disneyland "D" coupon. With a <span class="nowrap">3&#160;ft</span> (<span class="nowrap">914&#160;mm</span>) gauge, the most common narrow <a href="/wiki/Track_gauge" title="Track gauge">track gauge</a> used in North America, the track runs in a continuous loop around Disneyland through each of its realms. Each 1900s-era train departs Main Street Station on an excursion that includes scheduled station stops at: New Orleans Square Station; Toontown Depot; and Tomorrowland Station. The Grand Circle Tour then concludes with a visit to the "<a href="/wiki/Grand_Canyon" title="Grand Canyon">Grand Canyon</a>/<a href="/wiki/Primeval_World" class="mw-redirect" title="Primeval World">Primeval World</a>" dioramas before returning passengers to Main Street, U.S.A.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Disneyland_Mark_VII_Monorail_Red.jpg" class="image"><img alt="photo of new Monorail" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Disneyland_Mark_VII_Monorail_Red.jpg/220px-Disneyland_Mark_VII_Monorail_Red.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Disneyland_Mark_VII_Monorail_Red.jpg/330px-Disneyland_Mark_VII_Monorail_Red.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Disneyland_Mark_VII_Monorail_Red.jpg/440px-Disneyland_Mark_VII_Monorail_Red.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Disneyland_Mark_VII_Monorail_Red.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monorail Red travels over the <a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo_Submarine_Voyage" title="Finding Nemo Submarine Voyage">Finding Nemo Submarine Voyage</a> in Tomorrowland</div></div></div>
<p>One of Disneyland's signature attractions is its <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Monorail_System" title="Disneyland Monorail System">Disneyland Monorail System</a> <a href="/wiki/Monorail" title="Monorail">monorail</a> service, which opened in Tomorrowland in 1959 as the first daily-operating monorail train system in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>. The monorail guideway has remained almost exactly the same since 1961, aside from small alterations while Indiana Jones Adventure was being built. Five generations of monorail trains have been used in the park, since their lightweight construction means they wear out quickly. The most recent operating generation, the Mark VII, was installed in 2008. The monorail shuttles visitors between two stations, one inside the park in Tomorrowland and one in Downtown Disney. It follows a 2.5-mile (4.0&#160;km) long route designed to show the park from above. Currently, the Mark VII is running with the colors red, blue and orange. The monorail was originally a loop built with just one station in Tomorrowland. Its track was extended and a second station opened at the <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Hotel_(California)" title="Disneyland Hotel (California)">Disneyland Hotel</a> in 1961. With the creation of Downtown Disney in 2001, the new destination is Downtown Disney, instead of the Disneyland Hotel. The physical location of the monorail station did not change, but the original station building was demolished as part of the hotel downsizing, and the new station is now separated from the hotel by several Downtown Disney buildings, including <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Zone" title="ESPN Zone">ESPN Zone</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rainforest_Caf%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainforest Café">Rainforest Café</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DisneylandDriverMainSt_wb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Horseless carriage" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/DisneylandDriverMainSt_wb.jpg/220px-DisneylandDriverMainSt_wb.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/DisneylandDriverMainSt_wb.jpg/330px-DisneylandDriverMainSt_wb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/DisneylandDriverMainSt_wb.jpg/440px-DisneylandDriverMainSt_wb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DisneylandDriverMainSt_wb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main Street at Disneyland as seen from a Horseless Carriage</div></div></div>
<p>All of the vehicles found on Main Street, U.S.A., grouped together as the <a href="/wiki/Main_Street,_U.S.A.#Disneyland" title="Main Street, U.S.A.">Main Street Vehicles</a> attraction, were designed to accurately reflect turn-of-the-century vehicles, including a <span class="nowrap">3&#160;ft</span> (<span class="nowrap">914&#160;mm</span>) gauge<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tramway</a> featuring <a href="/wiki/Horsecar" title="Horsecar">horse-drawn streetcars</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Double-decker_bus" title="Double-decker bus">double-decker bus</a>, a fire engine, and an automobile.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> They are available for one-way rides along Main Street, U.S.A. The horse-drawn streetcars are also used by the park entertainment, including <a href="/wiki/The_Dapper_Dans" title="The Dapper Dans">The Dapper Dans</a>. The horseless carriages are modeled after cars built in 1903, and are two-cylinder, four-horsepower (3&#160;kW) engines with manual transmission and steering. Walt Disney used to drive the fire engine around the park before it opened, and it has been used to host celebrity guests and in the parades. Most of the original main street vehicles were designed by Bob Gurr.
</p><p>From the late 1950s to 1968, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Airways" title="Los Angeles Airways">Los Angeles Airways</a> provided regularly scheduled helicopter passenger service between Disneyland and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a> (LAX) and other cities in the area. The helicopters initially operated from Anaheim/Disneyland Heliport, located behind Tomorrowland. Service later moved, in 1960, to a new heliport north of the Disneyland Hotel.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Arriving guests were transported to the Disneyland Hotel via tram. The service ended after two fatal crashes in 1968: The crash in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Airways_Flight_841" title="Los Angeles Airways Flight 841">Paramount, California, on May 22, 1968</a>, killed 23 (the worst helicopter accident in aviation history at that time). The second crash in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Airways_Flight_417" title="Los Angeles Airways Flight 417">Compton, California on August 14, 1968</a>, killed 21.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_entertainment">Live entertainment</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alice_plays_musical_chairs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Disneyland Musical Chairs" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Alice_plays_musical_chairs.jpg/220px-Alice_plays_musical_chairs.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Alice_plays_musical_chairs.jpg/330px-Alice_plays_musical_chairs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Alice_plays_musical_chairs.jpg/440px-Alice_plays_musical_chairs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="853" data-file-height="639" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alice_plays_musical_chairs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alice and characters from her movie host "Disneyland Musical Chairs" at Coca-Cola Refreshment Corner, accompanied by a ragtime pianist</div></div></div>
<p>In addition to the attractions, Disneyland provides live entertainment throughout the park. Most of the mentioned entertainment is not offered daily, but only on selected days of the week, or selected periods of the year.
</p><p>Many Disney characters can be found throughout the park, greeting visitors, interacting with children, and posing for photos. Some characters have specific areas where they are scheduled to appear, but can be found wandering as well. Some of the rarest are characters like Rabbit (from Winnie-the-Pooh), Max, Mushu, and Agent P.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Periodically through recent decades (and most recently during the summers of 2005 and 2006), Mickey Mouse would climb the Matterhorn attraction several times a day with the support of Minnie, Goofy, and other performers. Other mountain climbers could also be seen on the Matterhorn from time to time. As of March 2007, Mickey and his "toon" friends no longer climb the Matterhorn but the climbing program continues. Every evening at dusk, there is a military-style flag retreat to lower the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_States" title="Flag of the United States">U.S. Flag</a> by a ceremonial detail of Disneyland's Security staff. The ceremony is usually held between 4:00 and 5:00&#160;pm, depending on the entertainment being offered on Main Street, U.S.A., to prevent conflicts with crowds and music. Disney does report the time the Flag Retreat is scheduled on its Times Guide, offered at the entrance turnstiles and other locations. The Disneyland Band, which has been part of the park since its opening, plays the role of the Town Band on Main Street, U.S.A. It also breaks out into smaller groups like the Main Street Strawhatters, the Hook and Ladder Co., and the Pearly Band in Fantasyland. However, on March 31, 2015, the Disneyland Resort notified the band members of an "end of run". The reason for doing so is that they would start a new higher energy band. The veteran band members were invited to audition for the new Disneyland band, and were told that even if they did not make the new band or audition, they would still play in small groups around the park. This sparked some controversy with supporters of the traditional band.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fantasmic_July_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Fantasmic" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Fantasmic_July_4.jpg/220px-Fantasmic_July_4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Fantasmic_July_4.jpg/330px-Fantasmic_July_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Fantasmic_July_4.jpg/440px-Fantasmic_July_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fantasmic_July_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Fantasmic!</i> finale on July 4, 2010</div></div></div>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Parades">Parades</span></h4>
<p>Disneyland has featured a number of different parades traveling down the park's central Main Street&#160;– Fantasyland corridor. There have been daytime and nighttime parades that celebrated Disney films or seasonal holidays with characters, music, and large floats. One of the most popular parades was the <a href="/wiki/Main_Street_Electrical_Parade" title="Main Street Electrical Parade">Main Street Electrical Parade</a>, which recently ended a limited-time return engagement after an extended run at the <a href="/wiki/Magic_Kingdom" title="Magic Kingdom">Magic Kingdom</a> at Walt Disney World in Lake Buena Vista, Florida. From May 5, 2005 through November 7, 2008, as part of Disneyland's 50th anniversary, <i><a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney%27s_Parade_of_Dreams" title="Walt Disney&#39;s Parade of Dreams">Walt Disney's Parade of Dreams</a></i> was presented, celebrating several Disney films including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Little_Mermaid_(1989_film)" title="The Little Mermaid (1989 film)">The Little Mermaid</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(1951_film)" title="Alice in Wonderland (1951 film)">Alice in Wonderland</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Pinocchio" title="Pinocchio">Pinocchio</a></i>. In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney%27s_Parade_of_Dreams" title="Walt Disney&#39;s Parade of Dreams">Walt Disney's Parade of Dreams</a> was replaced by <i>Celebrate! A Street Party</i>, which premiered on March 27, 2009. Disney did not call <i>Celebrate! A Street Party</i> a parade, but rather a "street event." During the Christmas season, Disneyland presents "A Christmas Fantasy" Parade. Walt Disney's Parade of Dreams was replaced by <i>Mickey's Soundsational Parade</i>, which debuted on May 27, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Disneyland debuted a new nighttime parade called "<a href="/wiki/Paint_the_Night#Disneyland_(California)" title="Paint the Night">Paint the Night</a>", on May 22, 2015, as part of the park's 60th anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fireworks_shows">Fireworks shows</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Disneylandfireworks.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Disneyland fireworks" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Disneylandfireworks.jpg/220px-Disneylandfireworks.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Disneylandfireworks.jpg/330px-Disneylandfireworks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Disneylandfireworks.jpg/440px-Disneylandfireworks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Disneylandfireworks.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Disneyland fireworks from Sleeping Beauty Castle</div></div></div>
<p>Elaborate fireworks shows synchronized with Disney songs and often have appearances from <a href="/wiki/Tinker_Bell" title="Tinker Bell">Tinker Bell</a> (and other characters) flying in the sky above Sleeping Beauty Castle. Since 2000, presentations have become more elaborate, featuring new pyrotechnics, launch techniques, and story lines. In 2004, Disneyland introduced a new air launch pyrotechnics system, reducing ground level smoke and noise and decreasing negative environmental impacts. At the time the technology debuted, Disney announced it would donate the patents to a non-profit organization for use throughout the industry.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Projection mapping technology debuted on <a href="/wiki/It%27s_a_Small_World" title="It&#39;s a Small World">It's a Small World</a> with the creation of <i>The Magic, the Memories and You</i> in 2011, and expanded to Main Street and Sleeping Beauty Castle in 2015 with the premiere of <i>Disneyland Forever</i>.
</p>
<ul><li><b>Regular fireworks shows</b>:
<ul><li>1958–1999 &amp; 2015: <i><a href="/wiki/Fantasy_in_the_Sky" title="Fantasy in the Sky">Fantasy in the Sky</a></i></li>
<li>2000–2004: <i><a href="/wiki/Believe..._There%27s_Magic_in_the_Stars" title="Believe... There&#39;s Magic in the Stars">Believe... There's Magic in the Stars</a></i></li>
<li>2004–2005: <i><a href="/wiki/Imagine..._A_Fantasy_in_the_Sky" title="Imagine... A Fantasy in the Sky">Imagine... A Fantasy in the Sky</a></i></li>
<li>2005–2014; 2017–2019: <i><a href="/wiki/Remember..._Dreams_Come_True" title="Remember... Dreams Come True">Remember... Dreams Come True</a></i></li>
<li>2009–2014 (summer): <i><a href="/wiki/Magical:_Disney%27s_New_Nighttime_Spectacular_of_Magical_Celebrations" title="Magical: Disney&#39;s New Nighttime Spectacular of Magical Celebrations">Magical: Disney's New Nighttime Spectacular of Magical Celebrations</a></i></li>
<li>2019 (summer): <i><a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Forever" title="Disneyland Forever">Disneyland Forever</a></i></li></ul></li>
<li><b>Seasonal fireworks shows</b>:
<ul><li>September–October <i><a href="/wiki/Halloween_Screams" title="Halloween Screams">Halloween Screams</a></i></li>
<li>Independence Day Week: <i><a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Celebrate_America:_A_4th_of_July_Concert_in_the_Sky" class="mw-redirect" title="Disney&#39;s Celebrate America: A 4th of July Concert in the Sky">Disney's Celebrate America: A 4th of July Concert in the Sky</a></i></li>
<li>November–January: <i><a href="/wiki/Believe..._In_Holiday_Magic" title="Believe... In Holiday Magic">Believe... In Holiday Magic</a></i></li></ul></li>
<li><b>Limited edition fireworks shows</b>
<ul><li>60th Anniversary: <i>Disneyland Forever</i></li>
<li>Pixar Fest: <a href="/wiki/Together_Forever_(Disney)" title="Together Forever (Disney)"><i>Together Forever</i></a></li>
<li>Get Your Ears On – A Mickey and Minnie Celebration: <i>Mickey's Mix Magic</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<p>Since 2009, Disneyland has moved to a rotating repertoire of firework spectaculars.
</p><p>Scheduling of fireworks shows depends on the time of year. During the slower off-season periods, the fireworks are only offered on weekends. During the busier times, Disney offers additional nights. The park offers fireworks nightly during its busy periods, which include Easter/Spring Break, Summer and Christmas time. Disneyland spends about $41,000 per night on the fireworks show. The show is normally offered at 8:45 or 9:30&#160;pm if the park is scheduled to close at 10&#160;pm or later, but shows have started as early as 5:45&#160;pm. A major consideration is weather/winds, especially at higher elevations, which can, and often will, force the delay or cancellation of the show. In response to this, alternate versions of the fireworks spectaculars have been created in recent years, solely using the projections and lighting effects. With a few minor exceptions, such as July 4 and New Year's Eve, shows must finish by 10:00&#160;pm due to the conditions of the permit issued by the City of Anaheim.
</p><p>In recent years, Disneyland uses smaller and mid-sized fireworks shells and more low-level pyrotechnics on the castle to allow guests to enjoy the fireworks spectaculars even if there is a weather issue such as high wind. This precedent is known as B-show. The first fireworks show to have this format was <i>Believe... In Holiday Magic</i> from the 2018 holiday season.
</p>
