<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tickets">Tickets</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DisneyTicketBook_wbelf.jpg" class="image"><img alt="old Disneyland ticket book" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/DisneyTicketBook_wbelf.jpg/260px-DisneyTicketBook_wbelf.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="103" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/DisneyTicketBook_wbelf.jpg/390px-DisneyTicketBook_wbelf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/DisneyTicketBook_wbelf.jpg/520px-DisneyTicketBook_wbelf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="316" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DisneyTicketBook_wbelf.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Disneyland ticket book circa 1975–1977. The tickets were printed as "coupons".</div></div></div>
<p>From Disneyland's opening day until 1982, the price of the attractions was in addition to the price of park admission.<sup id="cite_ref-book_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Guests paid a small admission fee to get into the park, but admission to most of the rides and attractions required guests to purchase tickets, either individually or in a book, that consisted of several coupons, initially labeled "A" through "C". "A" coupons allowed admission to the smaller rides and attractions such as the <a href="/wiki/Main_Street_Vehicles" class="mw-redirect" title="Main Street Vehicles">Main Street Vehicles</a>, whereas "C" coupons were used for the most common attractions like <a href="/wiki/Peter_Pan%27s_Flight" title="Peter Pan&#39;s Flight">Peter Pan's Flight</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Mad_Tea_Party" title="Mad Tea Party">Mad Tea Party</a>. As more thrilling rides were introduced, such as the <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Monorail" class="mw-redirect" title="Disneyland Monorail">Disneyland Monorail</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Matterhorn_Bobsleds" title="Matterhorn Bobsleds">Matterhorn Bobsleds</a>, "D" and then eventually "E" coupons were introduced. Coupons could be combined to equal the equivalent of another ticket (e.g., two "A" tickets equal one "B" ticket).
</p><p>Disneyland later featured a "Keys to the Kingdom" booklet of tickets, which consisted of 10 unvalued coupons sold for a single flat rate. These coupons could be used for any attraction regardless of its regular value.
</p><p>In 1982, Disney dropped the idea for individual ride tickets to a single admission price with unlimited access to all attractions, "except shooting galleries".<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> While this idea was not original to Disney, it had business advantages: in addition to guaranteeing that everyone paid the same entry amount regardless of their length of stay or number of rides ridden, the park no longer had to print ride tickets, provide staff for ticket booths, nor provide staff to collect tickets or monitor attractions for people sneaking on without tickets. Later, Disney introduced other entry options such as multi-day passes, Annual Passes (which allow unlimited entry to the Park for an annual fee), and Southern California residents' discounts.
</p><p>On February 28, 2016, Disneyland adopted a <a href="/wiki/Demand-based_pricing" class="mw-redirect" title="Demand-based pricing">demand-based pricing</a> system for single-day admission, charging different prices for "value", "regular", and "peak" days, based on projected attendance. Approximately 30% of days will be designated as "value", mainly weekdays when school is in session, 44% will be designated as "regular", and 26% will be designated as "peak", mostly during holidays and weekends in July.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Closures">Closures</span></h3>
<p>Disneyland has had five unscheduled closures:
</p>
<ul><li>In 1963, following the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">assassination of John F. Kennedy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1970, due to an anti-Vietnam riot instigated by the <a href="/wiki/Youth_International_Party" title="Youth International Party">Youth International Party</a>.</li>
<li>In 1987, on December 16 due to a winter storm.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1994, for inspection after the <a href="/wiki/1994_Northridge_earthquake" title="1994 Northridge earthquake">Northridge earthquake</a>.</li>
<li>In 2001, after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Additionally, Disneyland has had numerous planned closures:
</p>
<ul><li>In the early years, the park was often scheduled to be closed on Mondays and Tuesdays during the off-season.<sup id="cite_ref-GoCalifornia.about.com_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoCalifornia.about.com-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> This was in conjunction with nearby <a href="/wiki/Knott%27s_Berry_Farm" title="Knott&#39;s Berry Farm">Knott's Berry Farm</a>, which closed on Wednesdays and Thursdays to keep costs down for both parks, while offering Orange County visitors a place to go 7 days a week.</li>
<li>On May 4, 2005, for the 50th Anniversary Celebration media event.<sup id="cite_ref-DizHub.com_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DizHub.com-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The park has closed early to accommodate various special events, such as special press events, tour groups, VIP groups, and private parties. It is common for a corporation to rent the entire park for the evening. In such cases, special passes are issued which are valid for admission to all rides and attractions. At the ticket booths and on published schedules, regular guests are notified of the early closures. In the late afternoon, cast members announce that the park is closing, then clear the park of everyone without the special passes.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotions">Promotions</span></h3>
<p>Every year in October, Disneyland has a Halloween promotion. During this promotion, or as Disneyland calls it a "party", areas in the park are decorated in a Halloween theme. <a href="/wiki/Space_Mountain_(Disneyland)" title="Space Mountain (Disneyland)">Space Mountain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Haunted_Mansion" class="mw-redirect" title="Haunted Mansion">Haunted Mansion</a> are temporarily re-themed as part of the promotion. A Halloween party is offered on selected nights in late September and October for a separate fee, with a special fireworks show that is only shown at the party.
</p><p>From early November until the beginning of January, the park is decorated for the holidays. Seasonal entertainment includes the <i><a href="/wiki/Believe..._In_Holiday_Magic" title="Believe... In Holiday Magic">Believe... In Holiday Magic</a></i> firework show and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Christmas_Fantasy_Parade" title="A Christmas Fantasy Parade">A Christmas Fantasy Parade</a></i>, while the Haunted Mansion and <a href="/wiki/It%27s_a_Small_World" title="It&#39;s a Small World">It's a Small World</a> are temporarily redecorated in a holiday theme. The Sleeping Beauty Castle is also known to become snow-capped and decorated with colorful lights during the holidays as well.
</p>
